25:T4dc,You who believe, when you contract a debt for a stated term, put it down in writing: have a scribe write it down justly between you. No scribe should refuse to write: let him write as God has taught him, let the debtor dictate, and let him fear God, his Lord, and not diminish &#91;the debt&#93; at all. If the debtor is feeble-minded, weak, or unable to dictate, then let his guardian dictate justly. Call in two men as witnesses. If two men are not there, then call one man and two women out of those you approve as witnesses, so that if one of the two women should forget the other can remind her. Let the witnesses not refuse when they are summoned. Do not disdain to write the debt down, be it small or large, along with the time it falls due: this way is more equitable in God&rsquo;s eyes, more reliable as testimony, and more likely to prevent doubts arising between you. But if the merchandise is there and you hand it over, there is no blame on you if you do not write it down. Have witnesses present whenever you trade with one another, and let no harm be done to either scribe or witness, for if you did cause them harm, it would be a crime on your part.                   <foreign lang="ar">نَاحِيَةٌ</foreign> [app. as meaning The <hi rend="ital">vicinage,</hi> or the <hi rend="ital">quarter, tract, region,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">place,</hi> of a person or thing]: (O, K:) whence the saying, <foreign lang="ar">هُوَ عِنْدَ فُلَانٍ الآنَ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He is in the vicinage,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">the quarter,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">of such a one, now</hi>]. (O.) [See also <foreign lang="ar">عَنَدٌ</foreign>, which has a similar meaning.]       <sense type="A" n="2">-A2-</sense>  <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَ</foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30728-3" target="عَنْدَ" n="3" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> and   
      <foreign lang="ar"> <ref cref="n30728-4" target="عُنْدَ" n="4" type="1" subtype="WO" lang="ar"/></foreign> signify the same, (S, O, Msb, Mughnee, K,) being dial. vars., (S, O, Msb,) the first of which is the most common, (Mughnee,) and the most chaste: (Msb:) each is an adv. n. of place, and also of time; (S, O, Msb, Mughnee, K;) [used in the manner of a prep., though properly a prefixed noun;] of place when prefixed to a noun signifying a place [or anything local]; (TA;) of time when prefixed to a noun signifying a time: (Msb, TA:) denoting presence, (S, O,) i. e. perceptible presence, and also ideal presence, or rather the place of presence; (Mughnee;) and nearness, (S, O, Mughnee,) or the place of nearness; (Mughnee;) or the utmost nearness, and therefore it has no dim.; (T, TA;) [i. e.] it is primarily used in relation to that which is present with a person [or thing], in any adjacent part or quarter with respect to that person [or thing]; or in relation to that which is near to a person [or thing]: (Msb:) [thus it signifies <hi rend="ital">At, near, nigh, by, near by,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">close by,</hi> a place, or thing; <hi rend="ital">with, present with,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in the presence of,</hi> a person or persons, or a thing or things; <hi rend="ital">at the abode of</hi> a person; <hi rend="ital">at the place of,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">in the region of,</hi> a thing; or <hi rend="ital">among,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">amongst,</hi> persons or things: and <hi rend="ital">at, near, nigh,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">about,</hi> a time; and <hi rend="ital">at,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">on,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">upon,</hi> denoting <hi rend="ital">the occasion</hi> of an event or an action:]          <sense type="b" n="2">-b2-</sense>  using it as an adv. n. of place, you say <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَ البَيْتِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">At, near, nigh, by, near by,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">close by, the house</hi> or <hi rend="ital">tent</hi>]; (TA;) and <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَ الحَائِطِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">At, near, nigh,</hi> &amp;c., <hi rend="ital">the wall</hi>]; (S, O;) [and <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدِى زَيْدٌ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">With me, present with me, in my presence,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">at my abode, is Zeyd;</hi> and <foreign lang="ar">كُنْتُ عِنْدَ القَوْمِ</foreign> 
                  <hi rend="ital">I was with,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">among, the people,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">party;</hi> and] <foreign lang="ar">فَلَمَّا رَآهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">مُسْتَقِرًّا عِنْدَهُ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And when he saw it standing in his presence</hi> (in the Kur xxvii. 40)] is an ex. of its use as denoting presence perceptible by sense: and it is used as denoting nearness in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَ سِدْرَةِ ٱلْمُنْتَهَى</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Nigh to the lote-tree of the ultimate point of access</hi> (in the Kur liii. 14)]: (Mughnee:) you say also, <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدِى مَالٌ</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">With me,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">by me,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">present with me, is property;</hi> and meaning also <hi rend="ital">in my possession, and in my power and at my disposal, is property,</hi> though absent from me; <hi rend="ital">I have,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">possess, property;</hi> (Msb, Mughnee; *) and <foreign lang="ar">لِى عِنْدَهُ مَالٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I have property in his hands,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">possession;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">there is property due to me in his hands,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">possession;</hi> meaning, <hi rend="ital">owed to me by him</hi>]; as also <foreign lang="ar">قِبَلَهُ</foreign>: (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">قبل</foreign>:) hence it is used in relation to attributes; so that one says, <foreign lang="ar">عِنْدَهُ خَيْرٌ وَفَضْلٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He has,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">possesses, goodness and excellence</hi>]; and <foreign lang="ar">مَا عنِدَهُ</foreign> 
                  <foreign lang="ar">شَرٌّ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He has not evil</hi>]: and hence the saying in the Kur [xxviii. 27], <foreign lang="ar">فَإِنْ أَتْمَمْتَ عَشْرًا فَمِنْ عِنْدِكَ</foreign> i. e. [<hi rend="ital">And if thou complete ten</hi> years, it will be] <hi rend="ital">of thy redundant bounty;</hi> (Msb;) [or <hi rend="ital">of thine own freewill;</hi> as is implied in the explanation by Bd, and agreeably with common usage:] and it is used as denoting ideal presence in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">قَالَ ٱلَّذِى عِنْدَهُ عِلْمٌ مِنَ ٱلْكِتَابِ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">He with whom was,</hi> i. e. <hi rend="ital">who possessed, knowledge the of Scripture said</hi> (in the Kur xxvii. 40)]: (Mughnee:) [hence also] one says, <foreign lang="ar">لِى عِنْدَ فُلَانٍ حَاجَةٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">I have an object of want to be sought,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">required, at the hand of such a one,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">a want to be supplied on the part of such a one;</hi> meaning <hi rend="ital">I want a thing of such a one;</hi> as also <foreign lang="ar">قِبَلَ فُلَانٍ</foreign>]: (TA in art. <foreign lang="ar">حوج</foreign>:) [and in like manner one says of a right or due (<foreign lang="ar">حَقٌّ</foreign>): and <foreign lang="ar">طَلَبَ حَاجَةً عِنْدَ فُلَانٍ</foreign>

                  <foreign lang="ar">مِنْ لَدُنَّا عِلْمًا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">Upon whom we had bestowed mercy from us, and whom we had taught, from us, knowledge</hi> (in the Kur xviii. 64)]: (Mughnee:) [and in an ex. above, from the Kur xxviii. 27: and one says of a gift, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا مِنْ عِنْدِى</foreign>, meaning <hi rend="ital">This is from,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">of, my property;</hi> or <hi rend="ital">from me;</hi> or, by way of emphasis, <hi rend="ital">from myself:</hi>] one should not say [as the vulgar do], <foreign lang="ar">مَضَيْتُ إِلَى عِنْدِكَ</foreign>; nor <foreign lang="ar">إِلَى لَدُنْكَ</foreign>. (S, O, K. *)          <sense type="b" n="5">-b5-</sense>  Being a vague adv. n., (T, TA,) it may not be used otherwise than as an adv. n., (T, S, O, K, TA,) except in the following case: (T, O, TA:) one says of a thing without knowing it, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا عِنْدِى كَذَا</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">This is in my judgment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">opinion, thus</hi>]; and thereupon another says, <foreign lang="ar">أَوَلَكَ عِنْدٌ</foreign> [<hi rend="ital">And hast thou a judgment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an opinion?</hi>]: (T, A, * O, * K, * TA:) and in like manner one says, <quote>

                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">And who are ye, that ye should have a judgment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an opinion?</hi>]: (TA:) and thus in the saying, (Mughnee, TA,) of one of the Muwelleds, (Mughnee,) <quote>

                     </L> 
                  </quote> [<hi rend="ital">Every judgment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">opinion, of thine, in my judgment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">opinion, will not equal the half of a judgment,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">an opinion</hi>]: (Mughnee, TA:) they assert that <foreign lang="ar">عِنْد</foreign> in this case means the <hi rend="ital">mind,</hi> (T, O, * K, * TA,) i. e. <foreign lang="ar">القَلْب</foreign>, and <foreign lang="ar">المَعْقُول</foreign>, (O, K,) or <foreign lang="ar">القَلْب</foreign> and <foreign lang="ar">مَا فِيهِ مَعْقُولُ اللُّبِّ</foreign>; (T, TA;) [as in the phrase <foreign lang="ar">بُرْ لِى مَا عِنْدَ فُلَانٍ</foreign>, expl. in the S, in art. <foreign lang="ar">بور</foreign>, as meaning <hi rend="ital">Try thou,</hi> or <hi rend="ital">examine, and learn, for me, what is in the mind</hi> (<foreign lang="ar">نَفْس</foreign>) <hi rend="ital">of such a one;</hi> and in many other instances:] but this assertion is not valid: (T, TA:) [in a case of this kind] it means <hi rend="ital">judgment</hi> [or <hi rend="ital">opinion</hi>]: thus one says, <foreign lang="ar">هٰذَا عِنْدِى أَفْضَلُ مِنْ هٰذَا</foreign> i. e. [<hi rend="ital">This is</hi>] <hi rend="ital">in my judgment</hi> [<hi rend="ital">more excellent than this</hi>]: (Msb:) and <foreign lang="ar">أَنْتَ عِنْدِى ذَاهِبٌ</foreign> i. e.
